Page 13

Local News

A Glimpse of the Strict Preparations for September 7th

The military, police, and various agencies in this port, given the repeated victories on the front lines, are especially concerned about the defense of the rear. Moreover, the communist bandits in the three provinces of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi have not yet been completely suppressed. Shanghai, being a prosperous area for industry and commerce, is deeply concerned that communist party members may spread and flow into Shanghai, inciting strikes and class boycotts, harming the local area. Therefore, for several days, the defense of this port, especially in important areas, has been under temporary curfew in the evenings. Recently, an order from the Nanjing Headquarters stated that the communist party is plotting something in Shanghai, and precautions must be taken. Therefore, after receiving the order yesterday, the military, police, and various agencies have been under strict alert.

Ren Liping, the district head of the sixth district of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau in Caojiadu, Shanghai West, announced a temporary special alert starting at 6:00 PM yesterday. In addition to immediately notifying all sub-bureau chiefs, sub-station chiefs, and patrol officers under his jurisdiction to increase the number of officers patrolling in shifts for strict inspections and to strengthen defenses, he also ordered Patrol Officer Xu to lead a long police squad on patrol, traveling to and from Avenue du President Benes, Avenue Haig, and Robison Road, for strict inspections. Special attention was given to areas near factories. Liu Shaoqing, the leader of the detective team stationed in the district, also led all detectives to the key points for strict inspections, creating a rather tense atmosphere. It is also reported that there were similar alerts in the Zhabei area, and the 5th Division stationed there also dispatched a team on patrol.

Real Estate Association Opposes Water Price Increase

214 Representatives

Five Resolutions Passed

Regarding the Shanghai Municipal Council's proposal to increase the price of tap water by 25%, residents within the concession have expressed their firm opposition. The Chinese Ratepayers Association of the Shanghai International Settlement, acting on behalf of all residents, specifically convened a representative assembly at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce this afternoon to discuss countermeasures. The Shanghai Real Estate Association held a general meeting the night before, attended by 214 representatives from various real estate companies, including Shen Lianfang, Kui Yanfang, Shen Guangyan, Lu Shaotang, Ye Shantao, Dou Yaoting, Li Bohan, and Jiang Bingsheng, to discuss the opposition to the tap water price increase. Gong Kui Yanfang was elected chairman, and Tao Leqin served as secretary. The chairman delivered an opening speech, stating that tap water is a daily necessity for all residents and a public utility, which should not be equated with private profit-seeking enterprises. Therefore, the impact of a price increase would be significant, and residents were already strongly opposed. Furthermore, the original price of tap water was only 0.5%, and the price for foreign houses was 0.4%, and this had not increased for decades, but rents have continuously increased. Tap water prices have, in effect, been increasing every year. The 20% increase in 1927 was unreasonable, and now another increase is being proposed. There is no telling where it would end, which is unacceptable to the residents. Those present then engaged in discussion, resulting in the following resolutions: (1) The association will issue a declaration; (2) A letter of protest will be sent to the water company; (3) The Shanghai Municipal Council will be requested to reconsider the matter; (4) The Chinese Ratepayers Association will be requested to mediate, with the association pledging its support; (5) Letters will be sent to various organizations to represent the public opinion of residents and jointly strive for their rights. The meeting adjourned after the resolutions were passed.

New Director-General of China Merchants Group to Take Office

Li Zhonggong's Assumption of Office

Following Li Zhonggong's, the newly appointed Vice Minister of Transportation, appointment as the new Director-General of the China Merchants Group, Li has gone to Beijing to consult with Minister Wang on fundamental reforms for the group. He was originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai today to take office, and the acting Director-General Cai Pei was also prepared to hand over his duties. However, reliable information was received yesterday stating that Li is still in Beijing for negotiations, which have not yet been completed, and he will therefore not be able to take office in Shanghai as scheduled. It is now expected that he will be able to come to Shanghai to take office next Monday, the 8th. Acting Director-General Cai will go to Beijing immediately after Li's arrival.

Beijing Telegram

Li Zhonggong has been in Beijing for several days, discussing plans for the reorganization of the China Merchants Group and the Jinliyuan Wharf negotiation case with the National Government authorities and the Ministries of Foreign Affairs and Transportation. There are signs of progress. He will go to Shanghai to take over the matter in a few days.

Salary Payments to Staff

The group is two months behind in paying salaries to its staff and workers. After discussions between Acting Director-General Cai and Director-General Li Weihou, funds have been borrowed and delivered to the group. Yesterday, Acting Director-General Cai announced to all staff that one month's back pay would be paid today to help them maintain their livelihoods. Yesterday, all departments were preparing receipts in anticipation of receiving payment today.

British Minister to Come to Shanghai and then Go to Beijing

According to the "Shanghai Evening Post and Mercury", news received in Shanghai today states that the British Minister, Sir Miles Lampson, will depart from Beidaihe tomorrow (the 5th) to come to Shanghai and then proceed to the capital.

Ratepayers Association to Hold General Meeting Today

The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association will hold its third representative assembly at 2:00 PM today at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to discuss the opposition to the tap water price increase and the resignation of Chinese Director Bei Songsun. Both matters are important cases. According to a key member of the association yesterday, reports in the newspaper today stating that the association had already approved Director Bei's resignation are not true. Neither the Standing Committee nor the Executive Committee of the association has the authority to decide on the resignation of a Chinese director. The matter must be discussed at the representative assembly. Therefore, whether Director Bei's resignation will be approved is still uncertain and must be decided at today's representative assembly.

Postponement of Abolishing Likin and Implementing New Tariff

Due to the current situation, the Ministry of Finance's scheduled date to abolish likin and implement the national tariff will not be reached.

The Ministry of Finance's announcement to abolish likin and promulgate the national tariff was originally scheduled to take effect on October 10th of this year. That date is rapidly approaching. Although measures to compensate for the loss of revenue after the abolition of likin are being actively planned, the matter is of great importance and cannot be implemented in a short period of time. Therefore, there is a strong possibility that the scheduled implementation date will be postponed. A reporter from the Guowen News Agency visited a senior official of the Ministry of Finance at the Central Bank yesterday to inquire about the truth of the matter. According to the official, the current military situation makes it difficult for various provinces to abolish likin in practice. Although the business tax and other measures promulgated by the Ministry of Finance are good ways to compensate for likin, the ongoing military operations have prevented most provinces from implementing them. Even Jiangsu Province, which has begun preparations, has difficulty estimating when the implementation will begin. Therefore, given the current situation, it is impossible to meet the scheduled implementation date of October 10th. Consequently, the abolition of likin and the promulgation of the national tariff must be postponed until the twentieth year (1931).

National Goods Preservation Association Requests Implementation of National Tariff

The China National Goods Preservation Association recently sent a telegram to the National Government's Executive Yuan and various ministries, requesting the implementation of the national tariff, stating that the executive committee member Shen Shuyu had suggested sending a telegram to the National Government to promptly announce and set a date for the implementation of the national tariff rates by customs. This suggestion was approved at the 19th session of the 25th Executive Committee meeting. The current temporary tariff implemented by customs was originally intended to be a one-year trial, which has now expired. It is urgently necessary to use customs to protect the domestic goods trade policy and promulgate the national tariff rates in order to nurture the development of domestic goods and block a huge financial leak. The association respectfully sends this telegram earnestly requesting the relevant government bodies to review and approve the implementation and set a date for promulgation, so as to reassure industry and commerce and rescue financial resources. The association is awaiting orders with the utmost urgency.

Preparations Underway for the Third Annual National Goods Promotion Week in This City

The annual National Goods Promotion Week has already been held twice. The third event will soon be upon us. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has specially invited representatives from the Municipal Party Committee, the Municipal Government's various bureaus, and national goods organizations to form a preparatory committee to handle all preparations. The association's charter has been submitted to the Municipal Government by the Social Affairs Bureau for approval and record-keeping, and a temporary allocation of 3,000 yuan has been approved for the association's expenses. The publicity plan, in addition to generally following the methods of the previous event, also plans to hold a National Goods Fashion Exhibition to promote the joint participation of women in the national goods movement. With only one month remaining until the opening ceremony of the event on October 7th, the Social Affairs Bureau convened the first preparatory meeting with representatives from various agencies and organizations in the auditorium of the bureau on the day before yesterday (the 3rd). Those present included Hou Dachun from the Municipal Party Committee, Gu Zhu from the Municipal Government, Chen Jixi from the Land Bureau, Xiao Hongyuan from the Port Authority, Ji Xingjia from the Health Bureau, Jiang Zhihua from the Public Works Bureau, Wang Keyong from the Education Bureau, Sun Yimou from the Finance Bureau, Wang Guoxian from the Public Safety Bureau, Zhao Shutong from the Public Utilities Bureau, Zhang Quan from the Industrial Testing Institute, Lu Xiehua from the National Goods Exhibition Hall, Xu Genghua from the National Goods Preservation Association, Fang Jiange from the National Goods Federation, Chen Yiting from the National Goods Promotion Association, Zhu Boyuan from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Zhu Zhenhan and Ye Hancheng from the Machine-Made National Goods Factory Federation, Wang Hanqiang, and Wu Huanru, Zhang Tinghao, Dong Keren, Mi Jifang and Tian Heqing from the bureau, totaling more than 20 people. The meeting was chaired by Wu Huanru, with Wang Youfu as the recorder. Several important matters were discussed and resolved, such as the charter of the National Goods Movement General Assembly Secretariat, the outline of the National Goods Promotion Plan, and the charter of the National Goods Fashion Exhibition, all of which were thoroughly discussed and passed. It was also decided to hold the fashion exhibition at the Great China Hotel. As for the location for the opening and closing ceremonies of the General Assembly and other recreational and speech events, it was planned to choose between the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Auditorium and the Amusement Park of the National Products Commercial Association. The Secretariat will contact them and present the matter at the second preparatory meeting next week for a decision.

The Shanghai National Goods Factories Association held a meeting yesterday to discuss the issue of going to Singapore to open an exhibition. Over thirty people attended, including Xu Jianyuan. Japan Mail Company Suspends Many Ships and Reduces Services

A List of Ships Suspended on European and American Routes

After the Japan Mail Company added nine new ships this year, it now has ninety-six ships, totaling 613,000 tons. Due to the fact that the shipping industry in Europe and the United States is experiencing a surplus of ships and a shortage of cargo, the company has been gradually reducing services on various routes since last month. The ships that have already been suspended include: (1) Korea Maru, 11,810 tons; (2) Tianjin Maru, 12,420 tons; (3) Siberia Maru, 12,790 tons; (4) Kanagawa Maru, 5,851 tons; (5) Aki Maru, 6,022 tons; (6) Iyo Maru, 5,926 tons; (7) Sado Maru, 5,898 tons; (8) Awa Maru, 6,028 tons; (9) Kaga Maru, 6,512 tons; (10) Ceylon Maru, 4,950 tons; (11) Nagano Maru, 3,824 tons; (12) Tamba Maru, 5,844 tons. The total tonnage of ships suspended is 140,000 tons. There is no plan for the use of these ships.

Reduced Services on New York Route

On the Shanghai to New York route, the number of new British, American and Norwegian ships has greatly increased this year. The speed is extremely fast. Due to excessive competition, business has become slow. The company has decided to reduce four ships from this month, leaving only thirteen ships with a total of 55,500 tons traveling back and forth.

Japanese Again Refuse Large Numbers of Chinese to Return to China

After the Japanese authorities banned Chinese laborers from landing in Japan, all those who went were expelled. Overseas Chinese in Tokyo and Yokohama, due to the rising gold prices, and ending their livelihoods, were sent back to their country by the Japanese authorities in an unending stream. Recently, some Chinese going to Japan were strictly prohibited from landing by the Japanese coast guard. Chinese people in the Minamisenju area of Tokyo, Nanseicho of Kyoto and Fukagawa Hongo of Yokohama, who were engaged in hairdressing and the restaurant business, etc., were arrested by the Japanese authorities and driven back to Shanghai. There were also Liang Shaokui, Zhou Keqin, Hu Yinhe, Gao Jinsheng, Lin Wenda, Li Shanping, Liang Zhaozhen, Fang Azhuo, Le Quansheng, Xiang Kexiang, Yu Yufa, Tang Yannian, Zheng Baishu, Zhang Zhongbin, Xu Yaolie and dozens of others, who were expelled back to Shanghai in three batches. Most of them are from Qingtian and Guoxi in Wenzhou. They were all in dire straits when they arrived in Shanghai.

Foreign Ships Organize Security Detachments

Recently, because the central government's troops in Hunan and Hubei provinces are actively suppressing bandits, the British and Japanese merchant ships traveling on the Yangtze River are deeply concerned that dangers will arise. Therefore, they have successively requested and received the approval of their respective ministers to dispatch marine corps members to protect the ships. The Jardine Matheson Company, Butterfield & Swire, Nissin Kisen Kaisha and other merchant ships traveling on the Yangtze River will, from today, have temporary security detachments organized by the marine corps on board to provide armed protection.

Labor Dispute in Shipbuilding Resolved

Agreement Reached on Four Conditions

The workers in the shipbuilding industry in this city previously demanded improved treatment and submitted three demands to the Shipbuilding Industry Association. After declaring a strike on the 23rd of last month, the Municipal Party Committee mediated, and as a result, wages were increased by eight cents per worker, and work was resumed. However, the Shipbuilding Industry Association, as the ships being built were all commissioned by members of the Ningbo Coal and Stone Transport Association, then requested an increase of 12% in the construction price and an increase in meal costs from the association. As they had not sought prior consent, the Ningbo Coal Transport Association did not agree to the increase and requested compensation from the Shipbuilding Industry Association for the losses incurred during the strike, leading to a dispute. Yesterday, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce convened both parties to mediate. The meeting was chaired by Municipal Chamber of Commerce

Page 14

Representative Sun Mingqi. Both sides presented their arguments, and the dispute was quite heated. After Representative Sun Mingqi's explanations and persuasion, the following four conditions were signed: (1) Wages will be increased by eight cents per worker; (2) The Shipbuilding Industry Association should send a letter of thanks to the Ningbo Coal and Stone Transport Association; (3) In the future, any negotiations between the Shipbuilding Industry Association and the labor union must have the consent of the Ningbo Coal and Stone Transport Association; (4) The results of this mediation will be implemented starting from the 13th of this month. Both parties agreed to the resolution.

Overseas Chinese United Association Again Requests Repeal of Passport Law

Lists Ten Reasons

The Overseas Chinese United Association of the Republic of China, telegraphed the National Government yesterday, stating:

"Regarding the association's request to repeal the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' promulgated Provisional Regulations for Exit and Entry Passports, the Executive Yuan's reply, forwarded by the Secretariat of the National Government under document number 4974, instructs the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to reconsider. For returning overseas Chinese who are indeed impoverished and unable to pay the fees, the overseas embassies and consulates should be instructed to consider waiving the fees. The reply also states that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs intends to draft a passport law to address any imperfections in the provisional regulations, and once drafted, it will be submitted to the Yuan and then to the National Government for submission to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation and promulgation. Upon receiving this, we believe that the passport provisional regulations promulgated by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs impose excessive fees and contain many errors. Overseas party branches and overseas Chinese organizations have repeatedly appealed for revisions and reductions. The Central Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission also considers the passport law for returning overseas Chinese to be inappropriate and strongly advocates for its repeal. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs should understand the hardships of overseas Chinese and immediately repeal the law, stop collecting fees, and wait until a revised passport law is drafted, submitted to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation, and promulgated before implementing it according to law. However, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs does not realize its illegality and wants to protect its improper benefits. It uses partial fee waivers as a way to appease the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission's proposal to repeal the passport law, and uses vague phrases such as "(indeed impoverished)" and "(consideration for fee waiver)," giving unscrupulous consuls an excuse for demanding and nitpicking. Furthermore, it shows a lack of trust in overseas Chinese, suspecting that overseas Chinese who followed Premier Sun Yat-sen and supported the revolution are all pretending to be poor to avoid passport fees, humiliating the dignity of overseas Chinese. Overseas Chinese would rather die than accept such charity. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs treats the requests from various overseas Chinese organizations for fee reductions as insignificant and delays responding. It also allows lower-level officials of the ministry to collude with travel agencies to handle passport applications privately, extorting 26 Hong Kong dollars per passport. (According to the Batavia Tiansheng Daily and Surabaya Dagong Commercial Daily, Hong Kong's Anqing Hall and Guangzhou's Guangmeichang Zhong Junrao and others are colluding with lower-level officials of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to handle passport applications privately, charging up to 26 Hong Kong dollars per passport, as evidenced by receipts from travel agencies.) The association believes that this matter concerns the support of all overseas Chinese and dares not avoid speaking out. We respectfully present our loyal views to the government again: (1) All laws and regulations that increase the burden on the people must be deliberated by the legislative branch. During this period of political tutelage, the Legislative Yuan is specifically responsible for legislation. If the Ministry of Foreign Affairs believes that overseas Chinese, who have always had freedom of entry and exit, must have passports to be restricted, it should have carefully drafted regulations from the beginning and submitted them to the Legislative Yuan for discussion and revision. Instead, it violated procedures and privately promulgated the regulations, using the term "(provisional)" to try to cover up its mistakes. Moreover, there is no time limit for the so-called "(provisional)" regulations. When someone raises objections, the ministry presents a reply to revise them on one hand and vigorously collects fees on the other. There is no telling when the revision will be completed, and there is no limit to the burden on overseas Chinese. If no one raises objections, the regulations will go from provisional to permanent, and the Legislative Yuan will never know about this matter. Other government agencies will follow suit. The benefits will go to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, while the responsibility will be borne by the entire government. For the sake of respecting legislative procedures and maintaining the government's credibility, we must request that the regulations be strictly repealed. (2) The Central Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission has the responsibility of guiding and supervising matters related to the migration and protection of overseas Chinese. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs should have solicited the opinions of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission when drafting the passport law. Instead, it acted arbitrarily, privately drafting and promulgating the regulations, so that the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission could only send a letter after the fact to request fee waivers and could not express its approval or disapproval beforehand. For the sake of respecting the authority of the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission and maintaining the credibility of the party, we must request that the regulations be strictly repealed. (3) Most people who go abroad are seeking a livelihood. The vast majority of poor people are in this situation. Given the current preciousness of gold and cheapness of silver, even traveling in the lowest class of steerage requires several tens to over a hundred yuan in ship fare. Those going to the Dutch East Indies must also prepay an entry tax of 100 guilders, equivalent to over 140 yuan in national currency. Adding the travel expenses from the mainland to the port and the lodging tax for waiting for passports at the port, it already costs around 300 yuan. When begging is not enough, people resort to selling their property. When selling property is not enough, they resort to selling their children. Is such a tragic situation that moves even ghosts and gods not enough to move the pity of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs? Yet, it levies a huge fee of eight yuan under the guise of passports. Other extortions are even double that amount. Is this truly necessary for handling affairs? The Ministry of Interior Affairs only charges six jiao for issuing certificates of nationality and has even specially requested and received approval to waive the stamp duty. What the Ministry of Interior can do, can the Ministry of Foreign Affairs not do? Both ministries are located in the capital, and their cost of living should not be that different. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs only knows how to benefit itself. How can refugees escape with their lives? If they cannot escape, they will turn into bandits, and the bandits will multiply, leading to endless disasters. For the sake of maintaining the people's livelihood and reducing banditry, we must request that the regulations be strictly repealed. (4) Exit passports are required by foreign countries, while return passports are purely a matter of our country's sovereignty. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs uses the excuse that "(returning without a passport may disrupt public order)" and stipulates that "(citizens returning without a return passport will be detained and investigated by the customs at the port of entry)." This is intentionally alarmist and unreasonable. From a rational perspective, overseas Chinese returning to China is an innate right. What crime is there in not having a passport? On what legal basis are they being detained and investigated? If this is implemented, it will be treating overseas Chinese as specially prohibited items, giving customs officers the opportunity to extort money, forcing impoverished overseas Chinese to die in foreign lands, unable to return home, and treating them as outcasts like bandits, consistent with the exclusion policies of various countries. The government's "(Regulations for Encouraging Overseas Chinese to Return and Invest in Industries)" and "(Measures for Overseas Chinese Children to Study in China)" will be destroyed by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' passport law and will become mere empty words. Is it reasonable that the fervent support of Premier Sun Yat-sen by overseas Chinese is repaid with such cruelty? From a factual perspective, passports cannot determine whether a person is good or bad. Even communists will find ways to obtain passports. Setting up passports to protect good people is actually protecting communists. The Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission's proposal to "(exempt overseas Chinese from return passports)" is not without merit. For the sake of comforting overseas Chinese and maintaining overseas Chinese relations, we must request that the regulations be strictly repealed. (To be continued)

Labor Union of the Commercial Press: Declaration Regarding the Incident of American Citizen Running Over and Killing Lu Lianqiao

The Labor Union of the Commercial Press of Shanghai issued a declaration regarding the incident of American citizen Hays driving a car and killing Lu Lianqiao, an employee of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and the lack of trial in court. We respectfully inform all newspaper offices and fellow countrymen. Since the occupation of Chinese territory by imperialists, they have relied on consular jurisdiction as a protective charm, recklessly and violently harming people, disregarding the laws of the country they reside in, and trampling on national sovereignty for over eighty years. Recently, Mr. Lu Lianqiao, an employee of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, was returning home from work on August 7th, passing through the intersection of Nanjing Road and Shijian Road, when he was struck by an automobile number 11578 driven by American citizen Hays speeding from the west without sounding the horn. Mr. Hays should have braked and taken the injured person to the hospital for treatment, but instead, he sped away. Mr. Lu was seriously injured, his head and face bleeding profusely, and he immediately lost consciousness. Patrol officers number 542 and road patrol officer number 348 arrived, recorded the license plate number of the car that caused the accident, and sent him to Renji Hospital. However, due to the severity of his injuries, he died on August 11th. Although the court ordered Hays to compensate, Hays claimed the court had no jurisdiction, refused to admit fault, and disobeyed the order, treating human life as child's play. Tracing the origin of the disaster, it is rooted in the unequal treaties. From now on, we are willing to use our greatest determination to support the National Government's diplomacy and carry out the movement to abolish unequal treaties. In addition to petitioning the Municipal Party Department to forward the case to the Municipal Government to conduct diplomatic negotiations based on reason, aiming to achieve the goals of punishing the perpetrator and obtaining compensation, we hope that fellow countrymen from all walks of life will unite in resistance to uphold humanitarianism and protect national law. This is our declaration.

Respectfully, The Labor Union of the Commercial Press of Shanghai.

Special District Court Continues Hearing of Wu Suzhong

Headquarters Witness Appears in Court

Wu Denies Ever Knowing Him

Investigation of the Sandeli House

The Defendant Remains in Custody Pending Further Interrogation

Previously, the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, based on a report from an informant, stated that Shishi Xinbao reporter Wu Suzhong was an alias of the communist Hu Yu. Therefore, they sent a letter to the Special District Court requesting assistance in the transfer. Wu was arrested and the court has been opened several times. Wu absolutely denies his name is Hu Yu, and the court ordered his detention pending proof from the Headquarters for further verification, which has been repeatedly reported. It is now known that the case was continued yesterday morning by Judge Xu Jashi in the First Court, with prosecutor Xu Mei also present to perform his duties. In addition to dispatching legal advisor James J. Feng to the court to request the transfer, the Headquarters also sent investigator Wang Bin along with a key witness, Mr. Bao. Bao is a senior official in a certain organization. During his testimony, Judge Xu ordered that all those unrelated to the case be removed from the courtroom. He then questioned Bao, who stated that the defendant's surname is Wu and his name is Yu. Because in the spring of the sixteenth year of the Republic of China, Shanghai was still under the jurisdiction of warlords and the Kuomintang could not openly operate. At that time, I was a standing committee member of the 11th branch of the 5th District. The defendant's brother, Wu Guangzi, was a comrade of the 11th branch. The roster of party members of the branch was kept by the organization committee member surnamed Duan, but was unexpectedly seized by Li Baozhang. Li arrested all sixteen people according to the roster on February 22nd. The defendant was originally a member of the Communist Party living at No. 6 Sandeli, Baoshan Road, Zhabei, which was the general office of the Relief Association organized by the Communist Party, and served as the accountant of the association. His brother, Guangyu, also lived there. Li Baozhang arrested Guangzi, and the defendant was arrested along with him. I was held in the same room with the sixteen people. Through Guangyu's conversation in prison, I learned that the defendant was a communist. Later, because Li could not find the defendant's name on the roster, he was released on bail. Since then, I have never seen him again, and I have never met his brother Guangyu. Now I do not know whether the defendant has left the Relief Association and the Communist Party. When he was arrested by Li, the defendant changed his surname to Ye and disguised himself. His wife visited him in prison, but she did not recognize him. At that time, I deeply admired him. Later, attorney Ru Baoyi from the police and attorney Zhan questioned Bao. Judge Xu then questioned the defendant, who stated that his surname is Wu and his name is Suzhong, and he has no name Yu. He also has no brothers and has never been arrested. He does not know Mr. Bao, who testified in the middle of the questioning. However, as a news reporter, he has been to many places, and it is unavoidable that there are people who know him but he does not know them. But in the spring of the sixteenth year of the Republic of China, he was still in his hometown of Suqian. It was not until August or September of that year that he came to Shanghai. He has two brothers, and his brother's name is Shuguang, who is only sixteen years old now. There are six or seven distant cousins, but none of them are named Guangyu. He came to Shanghai to find a job, and he came with Zhang Yunqu. Because Zhang had a brother studying in Shanghai, he planned to ask him for help. Judge Xu ordered him to present evidence to the contrary, and instructed that if he had any questions to ask the witness, he could ask them. The defendant stated that the witness's words were completely unfounded. This is the third interrogation of this case. The officials of the Headquarters have stated each time that they have evidence. Today, Mr. Bao said that he and I were arrested by Li Baozhang. He allowed me, but this is absolutely not the case. I also did not join any party. I have never known about No. 6 Sandeli. Since the witness said that I lived there, the judge should inform the police attorney to immediately summon the landlord of the house to confront him. If they summon him after the court session, they may contact the landlord first. Judge Xu then asked whether he had any evidence to prove that he came to Shanghai in August or September. The defendant stated that he could only investigate his hometown. For example, the village chief Xu Wenle could prove it. He then asked whether there were any acquaintances in Shanghai, and when he started working at the Shishi Xinbao. The defendant replied that he started working at the Shishi Xinbao in August or September of last year, and it was introduced by Mr. Zhang. He knew Mr. Zhang through a pastor who introduced him, but he didn't know if he could still remember the date he came to Shanghai. Judge Xu then asked about the address of his first residence in Shanghai and the addresses he moved to later. The defendant replied that he first lived on Jin Shenfu Road, then moved to Xiaoshadu Maodeli and Laoshenfu Road Xinzhapu Road, etc. However, he either did not remember the house number clearly or did not know the name of the landlord. Afterwards, the witness Bao was questioned about the names and addresses of the other fifteen people arrested besides Bao. Bao said that he would submit the names of the other fifteen people separately to their respective residences. They are all scattered now and cannot be investigated. Jiang Jin, who was the propaganda committee member of the 11th branch at that time, later changed his name to Wang Ming due to the Communist Party, was arrested by the government and sentenced to eight years in prison, and is still in prison. Judge Xu stated that this case still needs to be investigated. In addition to instructing the defendant and his lawyer to present evidence to the contrary, he also ordered the investigator in charge to immediately inquire with the landlord of Sandeli about everything. Attorney Zhan immediately stood up and requested the court to instruct the investigator on the key points to be investigated: (1) Whether there was a Relief Association established in Sandeli in the spring of the sixteenth year of the Republic of China; (2) Whether there was an arrest incident. He also stated that in order to be fair, the Headquarters should send a special member to investigate together with the police, because the police are opposed to this case, which is unavoidable. Police attorney Ru Baoyi expressed opposition, saying that it is not useful for the Headquarters to assist in the investigation. If there is evidence, the police should sympathize; otherwise, it is illegal. Attorney Zhan immediately argued that if this case is illegal, then there are many illegal actions by the concession authorities, such as building roads beyond the boundary and Xie Huiyuan being sentenced to imprisonment by the Court of Appeal and released by the American Consul General. Is this legal? Moreover, the designated investigation location belongs to the Chinese territory. The Headquarters is the highest military authority, and the Public Security Bureau should be under its command. Why should the assistance of the Headquarters not be needed? Judge Xu instructed the police investigator on several key points of investigation, ordering him to investigate and report immediately. He will continue the trial after the case is presented, and the defendant will remain in custody pending rescheduling.

The Daughter-in-Law of Patrolman Li Qingfu Died Unjustly

Autopsy Conducted Yesterday Morning

Determined to Have Been Strangled

Li's Wife Still Claims Suicide

The Police Will File a Public Prosecution

After Li Zhangshi, the eldest daughter-in-law of Anhui native Li Qingfu, patrolman number 615 of the Gordon Road Police Station, suddenly died, it was rumored that she was murdered by her family. The police station arrested Li and his wife, Chen, along with their two sons, Yulong and Yukun, and sent them to the Special District Court for interrogation and detention pending an autopsy, as detailed in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that the police sent detectives to inform the Zhabei Police Station the day before yesterday, and then transported Li Zhangshi's coffin from the Yangchow Association to the Forensic Examination Office on Feilun Road. Yesterday morning, they summoned all the witnesses to the office. At noon, the Special District Court appointed Prosecutor Guo Huai-pu to lead the forensic doctor to the office. They ordered the workers to open the coffin and saw Li Zhangshi's body lying face up in the coffin, surrounded by lime and straw paper, with her face black as if it had been burned. However, the other limbs were also slightly decayed. The onlookers had differing opinions, with some saying that the body definitely did not die of illness, because the face of a person who died of illness would not be black. Then the forensic doctor began the examination. After detailed observation, he found wounds on her neck and arms, but because the body had been in the coffin for several days, it was difficult to determine. Then the forensic doctor saw that the corpse's mouth was open and the teeth were exposed. He used pliers to pull out a tooth and found obvious wounds on the root of the tooth. It was determined that the neck was a rope mark, and it was very deep. He reported his findings to Prosecutor Guo and determined that the death was not due to cholera. Mr. Guo then took a seat and questioned the witness, Mrs. Pan Wu, who claimed to be a tailor and a neighbor of the Li family. On the night of the 27th, the deceased was scolded by her mother-in-law, and the neighbors could hear the sound of cursing. Later, she heard that the deceased had committed suicide. Wu Genfa, a worker from the Zhang Wansheng Coffin Shop on Datong Road, Zhabei, testified that he went to the Li family to dress the deceased and put her in the coffin, and his statement was similar to what was recorded in yesterday's newspaper. Then the deceased's mother-in-law, Li Chen, was questioned. Because the coffin had been opened and the body had been examined, there was nothing to hide. She confessed that her daughter-in-law had hanged herself. She only had a slight quarrel with her, but her daughter-in-law was narrow-minded and could not bear it, so she committed suicide. When she found out, she rushed to rescue her and untied the rope. She still had a breath of air, but there was no way to save her. Later, her husband and son returned home, and her daughter-in-law died. She was afraid of being condemned, so she falsely claimed that her daughter-in-law died of acute cholera. Therefore, her husband and son did not know the truth at first. She explained to her husband and son after the interrogation yesterday. According to Li Qingfu and his three sons, they did not know that Zhang had hanged herself. When the incident happened, they were not at home. When they returned, they were told by Chen that their daughter-in-law had died of cholera. It was not until after the interrogation yesterday that they were informed by Chen. Prosecutor Guo then asked the forensic doctor whether the deceased had died by hanging. The forensic doctor said that the injuries were not consistent with suicide, but with strangulation. The wound on the root of the tooth was caused by yelling loudly when being strangled, and being punched, injuring the mouth or forcibly covering the mouth. After the examination and interrogation, Prosecutor Guo instructed the police to keep the body and coffin in the original place. Li Qingfu and his wife and sons were still detained separately. It is known that the police will file a public prosecution against Li and others, since the body was found to have been strangled, in order to uphold the law.

The Trafficker Dared to Offer a Bribe of Ten Yuan

Lin Yongfang and Chen Shaoting, investigators from the Women and Children Relief Association, went to the Xiamen liner Taiyuan, which was docked at the Swire Wharf in the French Concession, at 5:00 AM yesterday morning to investigate whether there were traffickers luring women and children to export. They saw a middle-aged man in the steerage cabin carrying a pockmarked girl about 13 or 14 years old, looking around suspiciously. The man claimed that the girl was his biological daughter, but the woman claimed that the man was her stepfather. Because their statements were inconsistent, the two were detained. Not long after, another man brought a girl about 16 or 17 years old onto the ship. It was observed that the man's eyes were agile and he was paying attention to the behavior of others. After repeated questioning, they learned that it was a trafficking case. Therefore, they took the two men and two women, along with the man and woman they had previously seized, to the Water Police Station for questioning. The Number of Dead Insect Egg Purchases is Alarming

Expenditure of 800 Silver Dollars

More Than 100,000 Pieces of Dead Insect Eggs

The Municipal Agricultural Experiment Station was ordered to purchase dead insect eggs to enrich the people's food. According to the report from the station to the Municipal Government yesterday, it purchased more than 160,000 pieces of dead insect eggs and more than 10,000 dead moths in the Yinhang, Jiangwan, and Caoging districts, spending more than 800 silver dollars. Each piece of insect egg can damage more than 100 rice plants if it becomes an insect. Although the cost of purchasing dead insect eggs last time was huge, the increase in production was considerable. It is now the breeding season for the three-spotted rice borer. The funds for this purchase are limited, and the reproduction of dead insect eggs is infinite, making it difficult to continue to cope. Starting today, the purchase will be reduced. It is now being sent to the Social Affairs Bureau for storage, and it is planned to select a date to submit a request to send personnel and invite the municipal committee members of each district to supervise the burning in order to encourage and promote the propaganda.

Abuse of Apprentice Actors

Bloodstains clearly visible on arms and legs

Already handed over to the District Court for investigation

A small teahouse in the market town of Caojiadu, Shanghai West, houses a Yangzhou opera troupe. They perform daily, and business is reasonably sufficient. One of the actors in the troupe, named Dai Lanfang, is 26 years old, from Yangzhou, and currently resides at No. 22, Xin Gongyi Lane in the town. At the beginning of last month, Zhu Yulong, who lived at No. 51, Xin Sen Lane, introduced Ding Li's son, Ding Heyao (11 years old, from Dantu), to Dai as an apprentice to learn singing. After Dai accepted Ding, the boy resided with Dai. However, for a month now, not only has he not been taught, but he has also been subjected to extreme abuse. Dai is also naturally tyrannical. If anything displeases him, he immediately resorts to beatings. This was known by the apprentice's friends, who repeatedly asked Zhu to negotiate with Dai, but Dai ignored them completely. One afternoon, around 8 o'clock, the apprentice dozed off. Dai saw this and first scolded him loudly, then beat him severely with a stick, striking him all over. The apprentice, in extreme pain, fell to the ground and cried out for help. Fortunately, neighbors saw this and, unable to bear it, immediately informed his father, who in turn asked the introducer, Zhu Yulong, to rush over. Zhu saw that Ding had already suffered several injuries, with blood clearly visible on his arms and legs. Zhu then called the police, who took Dai and Ding to the Sixth District Police Station. After interrogation by the District Chief, the case was deemed to involve an actor abusing and injuring an apprentice, a violation of ethical conduct. Yesterday, a document was prepared and he was handed over to the District Court for investigation.

Autopsy of a Lacquerer Who Committed Suicide by Inhaling Fumes

Li Er'a, from Wuxi, 31 years old, a lacquerer, was working in the Jia lacquer workshop at No. 31, Yu Deli, Beile Road in the French Concession. For some unknown reason, he suddenly had a momentary lapse and, on the evening of the third day at 8 o'clock, committed suicide by inhaling fumes in the workshop. When the poison took effect, his colleagues discovered him and immediately sent him to Renji Hospital. However, due to severe poisoning, treatment was ineffective, and he died at 1:35 a.m. the next morning. The hospital notified the French police, who transported the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall autopsy room. Yesterday morning, the French police criminal investigation department sent detectives to investigate. There were no family members present. Peng Hangen, a colleague of the deceased, was brought in for questioning. The coroner of the French Court, Judge Zhu, arrived and confirmed that the deceased had indeed died from poisoning. After questioning Peng Hangen, Judge Zhu ordered photographs to be taken and the workshop owner to prepare a coffin for burial. Subsequently, Wenyuanzhai provided funds for a simple coffin and the body was temporarily placed in the graveyard, awaiting identification by family members.

Result of a Young Woman Being Lured to Shanghai

Woman Dies After Divorce

Her Father Sues Her Ex-Husband to Recover Dowry

Zhu Genfu, a farmer from the 72nd Tu, 19th Bao, in the Nanhui County jurisdiction, previously sued his wife, Zhu Yu, at the county government for disobeying and verbally abusing her mother-in-law and other elders, requesting a divorce. As a result, the divorce was granted, and the dowry was ordered to be returned to Zhu Yu. However, before the lawsuit was concluded, Zhu Yu died of illness. Now, Zhu Yu's father, Yu Shukui, filed a lawsuit with the Nanhui County government against his former son-in-law, Zhu Genfu, demanding the return of the dowry (valued at over 900 yuan). After the hearing, Yu Shukui lost the case. Yu, dissatisfied with the judgment, appealed to the District Court, requesting the return of his daughter Yu Xiaomei's (i.e., Zhu Yu's) dowry. The appellee, Zhu Genfu, hired lawyer Xu Xingti to file a response. Yesterday morning, Judge Yang Keqian specially opened the Eighth Court to hear the case. According to the appellant Yu Shukui, after my daughter's divorce, all her clothing remained in her former husband's house. Now that my daughter is dead, her clothing should be returned, and I demand its return. The appellee, Zhu Genfu, testified that he is 24 years old and lives by farming. Yu Shukui is my father-in-law. The judge asked if all the clothing had been returned. He replied that all of it had been taken back by Yu. Asked when they were married, he replied that they were married twelve years ago, cohabited for one year, and on June 18 of the thirteenth year, Yu took her belongings back to her mother's home, as witnessed by neighbors. On August 19 of the same year, his father-in-law and others came to his house and took away all the dowry. This time, his father-in-law sued him for 900 yuan of dowry in the Nanhui County government, and the judgment was dismissed. Now he is appealing without any evidence. The judge asked about the divorce lawsuit, and asked who wanted the divorce. He replied that it was because she disobeyed and beat my mother, so I sued for divorce. The judge tried to mediate the case in court, ordering Zhu Genfu to pay Yu Shukui 50 yuan as a settlement. Yu Shukui firmly refused, demanding that all items listed on the attached list be returned in full. At this point, lawyer Xu made a statement. The judge, considering that the case still required evidence, ordered both parties to withdraw and wait for a continued hearing on a later date.

Public Utilities Bureau Does Not Allow Commercial Operation of Long Ferries

The ferrymen of the Lan Ni Du ferry were concerned that the Public Security Bureau's plan to take back the ferry and operate it officially would affect their livelihoods. They recently submitted a petition to the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, appealing for the reversal of the decision. A reporter from Huadong News Agency specially visited a certain gentleman in the Secretariat of the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau yesterday. He said that the ferrymen's petition had been received. However, this plan was entirely decided by the Municipal Affairs Conference. This time, the bureau's active progress was also due to the urging of the municipal government. However, the municipal government's eagerness to take back the official operation was purely for the sake of rectifying the long ferry crossings. The corruption of the eight long ferry crossings in the Huangpu River has reached its extreme. This undertaking concerns the lives of tens of thousands of travelers in the future. If it is not rectified, it will be difficult to fulfill the responsibilities of the municipal government to transform the city. Moreover, the Public Utilities Bureau's predetermined plan has also taken into consideration the livelihoods of the ferrymen after the official operation. The ferry business originally belongs to the city. The ferrymen mistakenly believe that it is a hereditary business, which is a mistake. Therefore, this time, the Public Utilities Bureau has rejected the request and will not allow it. It also said that the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau is also raising bidding on all construction and other items for the recovery of the Lan Ni Du ferry. It has been completed and is now starting to proceed. It is expected to be completed in February and March next year. As for the ferries built, they are also extremely complete, which is vastly different from the existing ferry operations. And the safety of passengers can also be absolutely guaranteed.

The atmosphere surrounding this film at sea has suddenly become cold. It is now scheduled to be screened at the Wanguo Grand Theater for three consecutive days starting tomorrow. Those who care about this film can finally stop waiting anxiously.

The Paris Grand Theater proclaims: Starting today, our grand theater will premiere the latest and greatest production from the Bird Film Company, "The Conflict of Flesh and Spirit." The stars are Lars Hanson, the protagonist of "Flesh and the Devil," and the beautiful actress Dida Barro. The play is adapted from the famous European novel "Anna and Carl," which depicts love and friendship in a passionate and profound way, which has never been seen before. It is said that it has been shown for three consecutive weeks in a major theater in Japan, and the box office has not declined slightly, which also shows the quality of the film.

The Star Film Company proclaims: The first grand martial arts film "Burning of the Red Lotus Temple," which is being produced continuously, has countless highlights. The recently completed fourteenth episode has even more extraordinary new features. There are many illusions, and the shooting method is special and unexpected. Now, as the release date of the film is very near, Qiu Yiwan, Wan Tiao Huan, and cameraman Dong Keyi are working day and night to rush production in order to complete it as soon as possible and give the audience a new perspective.

The fifth issue of "Era Youth" was published yesterday. Social News

Thousands of Unemployed People in New York are Trapped in Hunger

The number of job seekers is as high as more than 20,000. Female workers are willing to do any heavy work.

New York News: The Mayor of New York City, in order to alleviate the sharp increase in the number of unemployed people, has now opened a free job center. The number of job seekers is increasing daily. As of August 20, 15,000 people requested in writing, and 8,000 people contacted the center in person. Most of these job seekers have been unemployed for several months and are trapped in hunger and mental weakness. Thousands of people lined up and gathered silently. Even the police who were sent to maintain order felt bored. Among the 8,000 job seekers, 10% were women. They were willing to accept any low wages and heavy work. Among the 15,000 people who requested in writing, 648 people found jobs. Most of the people who found jobs worked for families for salaries of 30 to 40 yuan (including meals).

Japan's Gold Outflow is Approximately 200 Million

The Yokohama Specie Bank prepares to reduce its reserves.

According to Japanese news, since Japan lifted the gold embargo, a large amount of gold has flowed out. The total outflow in the second half of the year is not only the total amount of gold exported, which has reached 242,600,000 yuan, resulting in a reduction in the gold reserves of the Bank of Japan. On the other hand, the total amount of gold bullion flowing in from China's Northeast, Siberia via the Bank of Korea, the gold materials flowing in from Shanghai via the Mitsubishi Bank, and the gold bullion purchased by other gold producers reached 43,700,000 yuan. After offsetting each other, the amount of gold reserves is approximately 198,900,000 yuan less.

The Japanese Imperial Household Agency Photocopies Rare Chinese Books

Tokyo News: The library warehouse of the Japanese Imperial Household Agency has 220,000 volumes of books, including Chinese books that have now disappeared in China. In order to preserve and facilitate the academic community, the library has decided to reprint and distribute them to libraries and specialized schools. Considering the drawbacks of manual copying, such as omissions and errors, the original books will be photographed first and then printed using collotype. After the budget is set, it will begin next year.

China's Raw Silk Exports Greatly Increase During the New Silk Season

The Shanghai port has been relatively idle recently.

According to a survey by the silk industry, Chinese silk exports have greatly increased due to the benefits of cheap silver. From the beginning of the new silk season this year, from February to the end of July (Shanghai silk from June 1st to July 22nd, Guangdong silk from May 1st to the end of July), the total number of Chinese silk exports was 35,868 bales, an increase of 1,179 bales compared to last year. The most noteworthy point is that exports to Europe decreased by 2,057 bales, while exports to the United States increased by 3,146 bales, which is enough to offset the decrease in exports to Europe. This is solely due to the sluggishness of the French silk weaving industry. However, the export of Shanghai raw silk has recently become sluggish and there have not been many transactions. The reason is that the rise in silver prices and the increase in exchange rates since the end of last month have affected it.

Youth Garden

The Epidemic in Universities

— Ke

An epidemic can also be said to be a fashion trend. People who suffer from such a disease not only do not feel pain, but may even boast about being fashionable.

Indeed, we can now observe such a phenomenon in any university in Shanghai: writing love letters, watching movies, chatting idly, and strolling down the street.

In fact, it can be said that no matter whose dormitory you go to, you will always find very beautiful envelopes in his or her paper letter holder pinned to the wall. The envelopes are written in elegant penmanship, and the signature is either an English abbreviation or simply left blank. Similar letters with a mysterious color can also be found in large numbers at the gatehouse when the postman delivers them. Haha, if you open them one by one and appreciate them, it will really make you dizzy.

Saturday and Sunday are usually rest days, but university students who do not feel tired on weekdays, of course, do not need this kind of healthy moaning. Therefore, these two days have become their big gathering for watching movies. Lovers naturally come to the seductive cinema hand in hand, quietly indulging themselves. Those who have not found a partner can only lower their standards and invite a few friends of the same sex to appreciate the ardent love and intoxicating dance on the screen. When they come back or are about to sleep, they must start a fierce review of the movies.

Attending classes is, of course, absolutely free. Even in the lecture hall, their ears do not necessarily have to listen to the lecture. If they encounter a good professor, they will naturally pay more attention. If it is a boring one, the students will be impolite and start talking. The quiet ones are still talking and laughing softly, while the naughty ones simply open their throats and speak loudly. During self-study time, except for a few who are really studying, almost everyone is answering and laughing, talking about a certain classmate's family, or someone's love affair, or the cold or warm weather, or the quality of clothes, or the scenery there, or someone's appearance. It's all this kind of aimless talk. Although sometimes they will talk passionately and indignantly about social and national issues, or fierce arguments will occur due to disagreements on the main points—but wasting precious time on empty talk probably still cannot get rid of our unique national character of only talking and not doing.

After dinner, some students like to go for a walk on the street in groups of three or five. While chatting, their eyes keep scanning the people passing by on the left, right, front, and back, or unconsciously looking at the displays in the glass cabinets along the street. If a fashionable woman suddenly appears diagonally, ah, their eyeballs will seem to be sucked by calcium carbide, and they will never turn again. They must wait until her shadow completely disappears before they smile at each other, and finally add a few criticisms.

Of course, a dull and monotonous life cannot satisfy passionate young people—but, I think that at least when pursuing interests, we should think back to the future of our nation. Does it need this kind of anesthetizing adjustment? At the same time, we must deeply reflect on whether our current international position allows you to live in a muddle-headed way.

Here, I have an important thing to say, that is, under the current environment, we young people, especially the college students who are intellectuals, bear the great mission of promoting the nation and transforming society. What we need is not fun, but diligence and hard work, forging a firm spirit and a healthy body, preparing to shoulder heavy responsibilities in the future.

Mongolian Women

— Wen Juan

We, who are accustomed to living in the Jiangnan area with its beautiful mountains and clear waters, when we hear someone mention the word Mongolia, will immediately think of those vast and uninhabited wildernesses, the weather with flying sand and rocks, and the bitter cold scenes of snow-covered ground, and regard it as an uncivilized land that is not suitable for living in for a day. However, in the eyes of those who have been there, it does not seem so annoying, and perhaps there is a special charm worth remembering.

I went to Outer Mongolia in mid-August of the sixteenth year. The purpose was to investigate antiquities, but whenever I had free time from digging bones and pulling sand, I often paid attention to the actions of these so-called "Northern Rouge," as well as their joys, sorrows, customs, and habits. There are still some noteworthy places. Now, while this impression has not yet faded, I will write down a little bit for reference.

Preconceived notions limit our vision. We often think that only the Jiangnan area produces beauties. We don't know that among the women in the distant yurts, there are many "Northern Rouge" who surpass the "Southern Dynasties Jinpowder." Some of them have high noses like hanging gallbladders, paired with long eyes and large oval faces. The facial features are neat and reveal a refreshing and elegant spirit. They are tall and strong. From the perspective of evolutionary aesthetics, these are the unique advantages of Mongolian women, which our Jiangnan women lack. Every time I see their girls, wearing long jujube-red satin robes and a face that has not been injured by lead powder, walking towards me gracefully, it is as if a beautiful flower is blooming in the deserted desert where no one appreciates it. I am amazed at the impartiality of creation. Its gifts are not stingy due to the separation of mountains and passes. It is a pity that it is different after they become women. The scarlet red of rouge is applied to the skin, causing it to wrinkle, and the lead in the white powder turns the face yellow. Moreover, the hair bun on top of the head is not often combed, so that from a distance, it looks like a bird's nest. They are all very hardworking. All daily chores, such as picking up manure, milking cows, setting up tents, sewing clothes, and planting crops, are borne by them. The men do nothing all day long, just holding a dry pipe and sitting high talking or chasing livestock. Although they treat women, it is common to beat their wives with whips for no reason. They believe that a husband beating her is proof that he loves her. If a bride has not tasted the taste of a whip once in the past year, then she is an unfortunate person who is not loved. There was a Shanxi man who did business in Kulun who married a Mongolian girl. The girl's family was very well-off, but the dowry she brought to her daughter only included a fox fur coat and two pairs of cotton pants. The husband did not mind this and still loved his wife with the love of a Han man. However, she always felt depressed and unhappy, and others did not know why, or thought that her temperament did not match his. A nosy person used some method to anger her husband, so that he beat her after getting drunk. The next day, she held sharp scissors and tore apart the layers of cotton pants she was wearing. From the densely sewn cotton wool, she took out twenty silver dollars and presented them to her husband as an expression of her love for him. It was then that she knew that the dowry in these two pairs of cotton pants was quite a lot. The girl also boasted to others that her husband now liked her. This kind of situation... as long as you have lived in Mongolia for more than a month, you will know that I have not lied here. However, there are quite a few exceptions. The old women among them are also extremely fierce. According to custom, the northwest corner of the yurt is the place where ghosts and gods reside and is forbidden to people. If someone does not know and rashly sits in this sacred northwest corner, they will be politely pushed out, otherwise they will only be filled with old fists. Once, I was careless and violated the rules. The men were about to pull me. I had no choice and wanted to explain, but those men suddenly stopped and lowered their heads, as if waiting for punishment. I was confused instead. Suddenly an old lady with wrinkled face appeared at the door of the tent. She pointed at those people. As far as I could hear, it meant something like this:

"Without my order... she is a Han, dare you move a finger?"

Until I walked out of the tent in trepidation, their heads had not yet been raised. Presumably, this old woman is the head of the family. The dignity of women is old and eternal, and it is not inferior to the Han.

I really don't know where they get the strength to do so many things. Every time I see them dismantling yurts, loading cars, carrying odds and ends on their backs, and following the cars, walking seventy or eighty miles. After arriving at a place with water and grass, they have to set up tents, take care of children, and even bury pots to cook. Fortunately, their cooking is simple. Ordinary families always boil a pot of millet porridge first. When it's ready, they cut up some beef and mutton, throw it into the pot, and roll it slightly. Then they take it out and put it in a bowl. Fresh blood oozes from the meat slices into the bowl. This is what they think is the most delicious food. At this time, a group of men leave their cushions, put down their dry pipes, and eat these good things, never because the women are too busy and share a little of their hard work. Even so, they also have a little rest and happiness, which is the New Year and other festivals. Women in the village, except for the elderly, all wear red and green clothes, wearing satin hats adorned with pearls and jade, gathered in designated temples or yurts. Everyone dances and sings, from seven or eight people to twenty or thirty people. They hold hands in a circle, advancing and retreating, and there are certain rules. The singing sound is exactly resounding in the clouds. It is a pity that we do not understand what they are singing. Otherwise, collecting them would be a very good literary material. In addition, if there are distinguished guests, they will also hold family banquets and generally dance and sing, but the number of people is not that many.

Women usually also have their ways of having fun. When they go out to carry manure or milk cows, they always go together. When they have carried enough manure and milked well, they start singing in their spare time. The shepherds who collect sheep also respond to them. It is said that some are very good love songs, but we can't understand them. Otherwise, collecting them would be very good literary material.

Their social interaction seems very free. The boundaries between men and women are not very strict. Divorce is also very easy if the husband and wife do not agree. However, for the first marriage, the man's family must also lead a few sheep to the woman's family as a betrothal gift. The amount of this betrothal gift is not uniform and varies according to the family's circumstances. As for the man's family paying the woman's family a betrothal gift, this is certain. Presumably, these are the etiquette of respecting unmarried daughters. Remarriage is casual, without any formalities. It is enough if both parties agree.

Women can ride horses like men. The distance between their residences is very far. The scattered tents are scattered in the vast plain. Occasionally, when they go out to visit friends, they have to travel dozens of miles at a time. One day, I went to the home of an old lady named Kesh to find her daughter. I didn't find her. She said, "She went to Chuánménr (串門兒, visit relatives), I'll call her."

"How far is it?" I asked.

"It's just next door," she said, getting on her horse and leaving. In less than two meals, both mother and daughter returned. I learned that they were playing in a place twenty miles away. I couldn't help but gasp, "The horizon is like a neighbor's house," which can really be sung for them. If I could learn this skill of riding a horse, wouldn't I be happy? It is a pity that I still have to stay away from the little horses. Compared with these healthy women from the north of the desert, the cowardly Han people are really ashamed. It's just that I didn't stay there for long and set off on my return journey, so I couldn't do a systematic study of their lives. I still regret it when I think of it now.
